## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting mechanical stress (sigma) from strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which falls squarely in the domain of solid mechanics / materials science constitutive modeling. Temperature-dependent stress-strain relationships are central to thermomechanical behavior of materials, including elasticity, plasticity, viscoplasticity, and creep.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus varying with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for plastic deformation)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plasticity with thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (implicit nonlinear stress-strain, invertible form: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2))
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Temperature-dependent Voce: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - c2 * exp(c3 * epsilon)) (saturation hardening with thermal dependence)
- Johnson-Cook type (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (stress proportional to distance from melting temperature)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperature → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**n) reducing stress
- Strain hardening with saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) forms capturing diminishing hardening rate
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) representing initial yield before hardening
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-like exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) factors multiplying mechanical response
- Combined multiplicative decomposition → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable strain hardening and thermal softening
- Pre-strain or initial strain offset → (epsilon + c)**n shifted power law for materials with prior deformation history
- Phase transition or regime change → abrupt slope change in sigma vs T suggesting piecewise or sigmoidal T-dependence
- Concave-up vs concave-down strain response → power exponent c1<1 gives concave-down (hardening saturation), c1>1 gives concave-up (accelerating hardening)
